What techniques set it apart? </p></div><p class="right downloadbox"><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Infographic-EHGnsy5w1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="Ransomware Spotlight: BlackByte Infographic" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Infographic-EHGnsy5w1.jpg"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Infographic-thumb-kYmsJqA.jpg" alt="Ransomware Spotlight: BlackByte Infographic" caption="false" be_marvel="1" onerror="this.onerror=null;this.src='https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/Conti-infographic-thumbAR8mNYk.jpg'" width="178" height="285" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Infographic-thumb-kYmsJqA.jpg"> </a>View infographic of "Ransomware Spotlight: BlackByte"</p><p>BlackByte debuted in July 2021. Its first year of activity garnered the attention of the Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI) and the US Secret Service (USS). According to a <a href="https://www.ic3.gov/Media/News/2022/220211.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://www.ic3.gov/Media/News/2022/220211.pdf">joint advisory</a> by these two government agencies, BlackByte had already gone after at least three US critical infrastructure sectors (government facilities, financial, and food and agriculture) by November 2021.</p><p>This advisory shows just how BlackByte was actively establishing itself as a new noteworthy <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/definition/ransomware" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/definition/ransomware">ransomware</a> variant. On October 2021, Trustwave released a publicly available <a href="https://www.trustwave.com/en-us/resources/blogs/spiderlabs-blog/blackbyte-ransomware-pt-1-in-depth-analysis/" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://www.trustwave.com/en-us/resources/blogs/spiderlabs-blog/blackbyte-ransomware-pt-1-in-depth-analysis/">decrypter</a> for BlackByte. This however did not stop BlackByte as developers released newer versions that used multiple keys and <a href="https://www.theregister.com/2022/05/19/blackbyte-ransomware-attacks/" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://www.theregister.com/2022/05/19/blackbyte-ransomware-attacks/">ramped up</a> operations, going as far as to warn their victims against using the available decrypter on their website.</p><p>BlackByte’s emergence could be part of a larger scheme. With the purported shut down of <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/ransomware-spotlight/ransomware-spotlight-conti" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/ransomware-spotlight/ransomware-spotlight-conti">Conti</a>, researchers from AdvIntel surmise that BlackByte is one of the chief new ransomware variants <a href="https://www.advintel.io/post/hydra-with-three-heads-blackbyte-the-future-of-ransomware-subsidiary-groups" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://www.advintel.io/post/hydra-with-three-heads-blackbyte-the-future-of-ransomware-subsidiary-groups">part of its rebranding</a>.</p><p>At present, BlackByte continues to target organizations from all over the world. However, like <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/ransomware-spotlight/ransomware-spotlight-lockbit" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/ransomware-spotlight/ransomware-spotlight-lockbit">LockBit</a>, <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/ransomware-spotlight/ransomware-spotlight-ransomexx" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/ransomware-spotlight/ransomware-spotlight-ransomexx">RansomEXX</a>, and many other ransomware families, BlackByte avoids attacking Russia-based entities.</p><h2>What do organizations need to know about BlackByte?</h2><div><br></div><p>While BlackByte operators use their piece of ransomware in attacks for their own gain, they also run on a ransomware-as-a-service (RaaS) model for their affiliates. We have listed down the key highlights of BlackByte here:</p><ul><li><b>Initial versions used symmetric keys. </b>The earlier variant of BlackByte used the same key in each campaign to encrypt files. It also used AES, a symmetric key algorithm. This allowed researchers to create a decrypter to help BlackByte victims, thus forcing the group to change their encryption method in newer variants.</li><li><b>It has multiple variants. </b>The first known version of BlackByte was written in C#. Operators then released two Go-based variants. The more recent Go-variant was introduced around February 2022 and sported modifications particularly in its encryption algorithm.</li><li><b>Archives files using WinRAR. </b>In BlackByte campaigns data exfiltration is done before the ransomware is deployed. This is because the BlackByte ransomware is incapable of exfiltrating data, instead it archives files using WinRAR then uploads the file to sharing sites. </li><li><b>Uses trojanized <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/cybercrime-and-digital-threats/locked-loaded-and-in-the-wrong-hands-legitimate-tools-weaponized-for-ransomware-in-2021" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/gb/security/news/cybercrime-and-digital-threats/locked-loaded-and-in-the-wrong-hands-legitimate-tools-weaponized-for-ransomware-in-2021">legitimate tools</a>. </b>Like most modern ransomware variants, BlackByte uses living-off-the-land binaries. For example, it uses the remote tool AnyDesk to gain further control over a system and for lateral movement.</li><li><strong>Involves phishing emails or a known ProxyShell vulnerability for initial access.</strong> BlackByte has been known to use phishing emails or exploit unpatched ProxyShell vulnerability in Microsoft Exchange Servers to gain initial access into a system.</li></ul><p>BlackByte trajectory seems to point to continuing activity. In fact, reports indicate that BlackByte is among the ransomware operations that have set their sights on <a href="https://www.recordedfuture.com/latin-american-governments-targeted-by-ransomware" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://www.recordedfuture.com/latin-american-governments-targeted-by-ransomware">Latin American governments</a> in May 2022. This report is reflected in our own telemetry data as seen in the next section.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="full-width-block normalStyleBlock"><h2 class="centeredBlock margin-topAdjust">Top affected industries and countries</h2><!--content--><div class="width-90-wide margin-bottomAdjust"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-2-col-layout"><div class="grid-col"><p>The data used in this section represent the count of unique machines where BlackByte-related activity had been detected. Based on our telemetry data, BlackByte showed a fairly consistent level of activity from October 2021 to March 2022. However, May 2022 detections showed a drastic uptick in number.</p><p><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-1-HYAXKRn.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="BlackByte monthly unique detections  (October 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022)" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-1-HYAXKRn.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-1-HYAXKRn.png" caption="false" width="554" height="304" alt="BlackByte monthly unique detections  (October 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022)" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-1-HYAXKRn.png"></a></p><p class="smallText">Figure 1. BlackByte monthly unique detections  (October 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022)<br><em>Source: Trend Micro™ Smart Protection Network™</em></p></div><div class="grid-col"><p>Based on our telemetry data from April 30, 2021 to May 31, 2022, we detected BlackByte activity all over the globe. However, after the spike in activity in May, Peru outstripped other countries in detection. This is consistent with the <a href="https://www.recordedfuture.com/latin-american-governments-targeted-by-ransomware" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://www.recordedfuture.com/latin-american-governments-targeted-by-ransomware">reported escalation of ransomware attacks</a> in Latin America, where BlackByte was also reportedly among those that targeted the region.  <br><o:p></o:p></p><p><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-2-0fWUgZy.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="Countries with the highest number of attack attempts for the BlackByte ransomware (April 30, 2021 to May 30, 2022)" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-2-0fWUgZy.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-2-0fWUgZy.png?v1.1" width="1000" height="550" caption="false" alt="Countries with the highest number of attack attempts for the BlackByte ransomware (April 30, 2021 to May 30, 2022)" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-2-0fWUgZy.png?v1.1"></a></p><p class="smallText">Figure 2. Countries with the highest number of attack attempts for the BlackByte ransomware (April 30, 2021 to May 30, 2022)<br><em>Source: Trend Micro Smart Protection Network</em></p></div></div><div class="grid-1-col-layout" style="margin: 0 auto;" data-mce-style="margin: 0 auto;"><div class="grid-col"><p>Up to the end of April 2022, the technology sector saw the most BlackByte detections, however, in May, detections in the government sector also shot up.</p><p><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-3-fTWT0rk.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="Countries with the highest number of attack attempts for the BlackByte ransomware (April 30, 2021 to May 30, 2022)" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-3-fTWT0rk.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-3-fTWT0rk.png?v1.1" alt="Countries with the highest number of attack attempts for the BlackByte ransomware (April 30, 2021 to May 30, 2022)" width="698" height="384" caption="false" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-3-fTWT0rk.png?v1.1"></a></p><p class="smallText">Figure 3. Countries with the highest number of attack attempts for the BlackByte ransomware (April 30, 2021 to May 30, 2022)<br><em style="font-size: 13px; letter-spacing: 0.5px;" data-mce-style="font-size: 13px; letter-spacing: 0.5px;">Source: Trend Micro Smart Protection Network</em></p><p>One way to interpret these observations is that the drastic increase stemmed from a single attack that affected several machines. Aside from the reports on ransomware groups targeting Latin America, this explanation is also based on the report that, by their own claim, BlackByte operators had compromised a Peruvian government entity around the time of the increased activity.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="full-width-block normalStyleBlock"><h2 class="centeredBlock margin-topAdjust">Targeted regions and sectors according to BlackByte leaksite</h2><!--content--><div class="width-90-wide margin-bottomAdjust"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-2-col-layout"><div class="grid-col"><p><!-- x-tinymce/html -->In addition to these detections, we delved into BlackByte’s leak site to see the number of attacks recorded there. We looked at data from August 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022. Based on what we found in the site, BlackByte’s victims were composed mostly of small size businesses. The activity peaked in November 2021.</p><p>Overall, the leak site has yet to reflect the focused attack on Latin American governments. The distribution of their attacks per region showed, instead, a proclivity for targeting entities based in North America and Europe. </p><p><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-4-Eswra13.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="Regional distribution of BlackByte victims according to the group’s leak site (August 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022)" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-4-Eswra13.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-4-Eswra13.png?v1.1" caption="false" width="554" height="304" alt="Regional distribution of BlackByte victims according to the group’s leak site (August 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022)" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-4-Eswra13.png?v1.1"></a></p><p class="smallText">Figure 4. Regional distribution of BlackByte victims according to the group’s leak site (August 1, 2021 to May 31, 2022)</p></div><div class="grid-col"><p>Based on the leak site data alone, BlackByte operators and their affiliates have yet to show a marked interest in any one sector. We found a relatively even distribution of attacks across industries, which included the following:</p><ul><li>Construction</li><li>Materials</li><li>Healthcare</li><li>Retail</li><li>Transportation</li><li>Energy & Utilities</li><li>Manufacturing</li><li>Professional services</li><li>Automobile</li><li>Community</li><li>Foods & Staples</li><li>Real Estate</li><li>Government</li><li>IT</li><li>Legal services</li><li>Media and entertainment</li></ul></div></div><div class="grid-1-col-layout" style="margin: 0 auto;" data-mce-style="margin: 0 auto;"><div class="grid-col">Comparing the leak site data of BlackByte to other ransomware families, shows that from January 1, 2022 to May 31, 2022, BlackByte was among the 10 ransomware groups with the greatest number of self-reported victims.<o:p></o:p><p><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-5-MBFGTGm.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener" title="Top ransomware groups with the greatest number of listed victims in their respective leak sites (January 1, 2022 to May 31, 2022)" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-5-MBFGTGm.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-5-MBFGTGm.png?v1.1" alt="Top ransomware groups with the greatest number of listed victims in their respective leak sites (January 1, 2022 to May 31, 2022)" width="698" height="384" caption="false" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-5-MBFGTGm.png?v1.1"></a></p><p class="smallText">Figure 5. Top ransomware groups with the greatest number of listed victims in their respective leak sites (January 1, 2022 to May 31, 2022)</p><p>The data seems to show that BlackByte's operation is beginning to build a name for itself in the threat landscape while still building momentum. The following section shows how it works and how it conducts its attacks.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="full-width-block normalStyleBlock"><h2 class="centeredBlock margin-topAdjust">Infection chain and techniques</h2><div class="width-90-wide margin-bottomAdjust"><div class="wide-padding maxWidth900"><p>Given that BlackByte operates on the RaaS model, its infection chain can vary depending on the target. </p><p><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-6-wLJOoZX.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-6-wLJOoZX.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-6-wLJOoZX.png?v1.1" caption="false" width="876" height="407" alt="BlackByte infection chain" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-6-wLJOoZX.png?v1.1"></a></p><p class="smallText">Figure 6. BlackByte infection chain</p></div></div></div><div class="cardStackSection"><div class="full-width-block height_80vh deckEffectBlock"><div class="tableBlockholder"><div class="tableCellBlockholder"><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-2-col-layout"><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder server-db-control"><br></div><h4>Initial Access</h4><ul><li>BlackByte can arrive in a system by exploiting the ProxyShell vulnerabilities. Exploiting the vulnerable server allows the attacker to create a web shell to the system which is then used to download and drop Cobeacon using Certutil.</li><li>After the initial access into the system, the attackers use Certutil to download and execute the components that it needs to propagate in the network.</li><li>After the deployment of Cobeacon, it is then used to execute BlackByte ransomware.</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder defense-evasion-icon"><br></div><h4>Discovery and Lateral Movement</h4><ul><li>Based on our data, the actors used NetScan as a network discovery tool that allows the attackers to get a good view of the victim’s network environment.</li><li>After network reconnaissance, the attackers deploy AnyDesk in the system for an additional level of control over the system. The attackers repeat this process of discovery and deployment of Cobeacon and AnyDesk until it achieves its goals.</li><li>During the execution of BlackByte, it terminates certain processes and services related to security application to evade detection.</li></ul></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="full-width-block height_80vh deckEffectBlock"><div class="tableBlockholder"><div class="tableCellBlockholder"><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-2-col-layout"><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder exfiltration-icon"><br></div><h4>Exfiltration</h4><ul><li>Once the attackers have sufficiently infiltrated into the victim’s network and identified valuable files, it exfiltrates them using WinRar to archive the files and upload them into file sharing sites such as anonymfiles[.]com and file[.]io.</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder discovery-icon"><br></div><h4>Impact</h4><ul><li>Once the ransomware is executed, it terminates certain services and processes related to security application to evade detections. It also connects to its C&C server where it looks for a certain PNG file that contains information critical to encryption and is used to derive the AES128 key. This key is then protected using an embedded RSA key which will then become undecryptable without the private key. The ransomware then deletes shadow copies in the system using vssadmin.<br><br><a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-7-wWQCX82.png" title="Sample ransom note" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-7-wWQCX82.png"><img src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-7-wWQCX82.png" width="246" height="215" caption="false" style="width: 346px; display: block; margin: 0px auto 0px auto;" alt="Sample ransom note" data-mce-src="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/RS-BlackByte-Fig-7-wWQCX82.png" data-mce-style="width: 346px; display: block; margin: 0px auto 0px auto;"></a><p class="smallText">Figure 7. Sample ransom note</p></li></ul></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="full-width-block height_80vh deckEffectBlock height_auto_max"><div class="tableBlockholder"><div class="tableCellBlockholder"><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-1-col-layout"><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder execution-icon"><br></div><h4>Other technical details</h4><ul><li>It avoids encrypting the following files with strings in their file name:<div class="grid-2-col-count"><ul class="grid-col-layout no-margin-top"><li>obamka.js</li><li>thumbs.db</li><li>ntdetect.com</li><li>ntuser.dat.log</li><li>bootnxt</li><li>bootsect.bak</li><li>ntldr</li><li>autoexec.bat</li><li>Recycle.Bin</li><li>iconcache.db</li><li>bootmgr</li><li>bootfont.bin</li></ul></div></li><li>It avoids encrypting files with the following extensions:<div class="grid-3-col-count"><ul class="grid-col-layout no-margin-top"><li>msilog</li><li>log</li><li>ldf</li><li>lock</li><li>theme</li><li>msi</li><li>sys</li><li>wpx</li><li>cpl</li><li>adv</li><li>msc</li><li>scr</li><li>key</li><li>ico</li><li>dll</li><li>hta</li><li>deskthemepack</li><li>nomedia</li><li>msu</li><li>rtp</li><li>msp</li><li>idx</li><li>ani</li><li>386</li><li>diagcfg</li><li>bin</li><li>mod</li><li>ics</li><li>com</li><li>hlp</li><li>spl</li><li>nls</li><li>cab</li><li>exe</li><li>diagpkg</li><li>icl</li><li>ocx</li><li>rom</li><li>prf</li><li>themepack</li><li>msstyles</li><li>icns</li><li>mpa</li><li>drv</li><li>cur</li><li>diagcab</li><li>cmd</li><li>shs</li></ul></div></li><li>It terminates the following services:<div class="grid-3-col-count"><ul class="grid-col-layout no-margin-top"><li>SQLTELEMETRY</li><li>SQLTELEMETRY$ECWDB2</li><li>SQLWriter</li><li>SstpSvc</li><li>MBAMService</li><li>wuauserv</li></ul></div></li><li>It terminates the following processes if found in the affected system’s memory:<div class="grid-3-col-count"><ul class="grid-col-layout no-margin-top"><li>agntsvc</li><li>CNTAoSMgr</li><li>dbeng50</li><li>dbsnmp</li><li>encsvc</li><li>excel</li><li>firefox</li><li>firefoxconfig</li><li>infopath</li><li>isqlplussvc</li><li>mbamtray</li><li>msaccess</li><li>msftesql</li><li>mspub</li><li>mydesktopqos</li><li>mydesktopservice</li><li>mysqld</li><li>mysqld-nt</li><li>mysqld-opt</li><li>Ntrtscan</li><li>ocautoupds</li><li>ocomm</li><li>ocssd</li><li>onenote</li><li>oracle</li><li>outlook</li><li>PccNTMon</li><li>powerpnt</li><li>sqbcoreservice</li><li>sql</li><li>sqlagent</li><li>sqlbrowser</li><li>sqlservr</li><li>sqlwriter</li><li>steam</li><li>synctime</li><li>tbirdconfig</li><li>thebat</li><li>thebat64</li><li>thunderbird</li><li>tmlisten</li><li>visio</li><li>winword</li><li>wordpad</li><li>xfssvccon</li><li>zoolz</li><li>anydesk</li><li>chrome</li><li>opera</li><li>msedge</li><li>firefox</li><li>iexplore</li><li>explorer</li><li>winlogon</li><li>SearchIndexer</li><li>wininit</li><li>SearchApp</li><li>SearchUI</li><li>Powershel</li></ul></div></li></ul></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="full-width-block deckEffectBlock bgcolorvar_1 normalStyleBlock fullWidthGray"><h2 class="centeredBlock margin-topAdjust">MITRE tactics and techniques</h2><div class="tableWrapper"><table class="tableContentDarkTheme mitreTableStyle mce-item-table"><thead><tr><th>Initial Access</th><th>Persistence</th><th>Privilege Escalation</th><th>Defense Evasion</th><th>Discovery</th><th>Lateral Movement</th><th>Collection</th><th>Exfiltration</th><th>Command and Control </th><th>Impact</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><p><strong>T1190</strong> - Exploit Public-Facing Application<br><em><em>It has been observed to be using the ProxyShell exploit to deliver China Chopper web shell as its initial arrival.</em></em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1053.005</strong> - Scheduled Task/Job: Scheduled Task<br><em>It creates a scheduled task to execute its java script to proceed with its routine on bootup. <br><em style="display: inline !important;" data-mce-style="display: inline !important;">Task Name: Joke<br></em><em style="display: inline !important;" data-mce-style="display: inline !important;">Trigger: Once, at 00:00<br></em><em style="display: inline !important;" data-mce-style="display: inline !important;">Action: wscript.exe <Malware Path and Name></em></em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1134</strong> - Access Token Manipulation<br><em>This ransomware modifies the registry to elevate local privilege and enable linked connections.</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1140</strong> - Deobfuscate/Decode Files or Information<br><em><em>It initially arrives as an obfuscated Java Script file which will be decoded upon execution. </em></em></p><p><strong>T1222</strong> - File and Directory Permissions Modification<em>It uses mountvol.exe to mount volume names and icacls.exe to modify the access on the volume to "Everyone."<br><br>C:\Windows\System32\icacls.exe" "C:*" /grant Everyone:F /T /C /Q <br><br>It also controlled folder access using PowerShell:<br><br><em>"C:\Windows\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe" Set-MpPreference -EnableControlledFolderAccess Disabled </em><br><br>It also modifies firewall settings to enable linked connections:<br><br><em>"C:\Windows\System32\netsh.exe" advfirewall firewall set rule group="Network Discovery" new enable=Yes </em><em>"C:\Windows\System32\netsh.exe" advfirewall firewall set rule group="File and Printer Sharing" new enable=Yes </em></em></p><p><strong>T1562.001</strong> - Impair Defenses: Disable or Modify Tools<br><em>It disables Raccine, which is an anti-ransomware utility, using these commands:<br> <br>taskill.exe /F /IM Raccine.exe<br>taskill.exe /F /IM RaccineSettings.exe<br>schtasks.exe /DELETE /TN \"Raccine Rules Updater\" /F<br>Deletes raccine autostart:<br><br>HKCU\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run<br>Name = “Raccine Tray”<br>HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\EventLog\Application\Raccine</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1083</strong> - File and Directory Discovery<br><em>This ransomware discovers files and directories by first enumerating the logical drives. Once enumerated, it then changes the access control of files and directories so that it can have full access over them. It will then go through the directories and traverse it for target files to encrypt.</em></p><p><strong>T1069.002</strong> - Permission Groups Discovery: Domain Groups<br><em>It uses the RootDSE entry from the active directory to get a listing of the hostname under that domain in preparation for its propagation in the network. It enumerates 1000 hostname in the domain.<br></em><br>Remote System Discovery<br><em>After getting the hostname of the remote systems, it attempts to ping the systems to see if it is alive and accessible. Then it proceeds with the transfer to the public share folder.</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1570</strong> - Lateral Tool Transfer<br><em>It checks if this folder is present:<br>C:\Users\Public\blockator  (infection marker for that system)<br>It doesnt proceed to propagation if it exist.<br><br>It checks the remote system if either of the following folders is accessible:<br>\C$\Users\Public<br>\Users\Public<br><br>It then creates the infection marker on that system, which are:<br>\Users\Public\blockator<br>\C$\Users\Public\blockator<br><br>It then copies the initial js file in the remote to Public share and executes it through scheduled task, which was created at the start of routine.</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1560.001</strong> - Archive Collected Data: Archive via Utility<br><em>It uses WinRar to archive files before uploading to its cloud storage.</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1567</strong> - Exfiltration Over Web Service <br><em>It uses WinRar to archive files and upload to cloud storage, which are:  <br>    - anonymfiles[.]com<br>    - file[.]io</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1071.001</strong> - Application Layer Protocol: Web Protocols<br><em>The payload is executed via evaluating an HTTP post through the “Request.Item” commandlet.<br><br>For BLACKBYTE v1, it uses the HTTP protocol to communicate with an adversary-controlled server to obtain the key it uses for encryption. The servers are:<br> - hxxp://45[.]9.148.114/forest.png <br> - hxxp://185[.]93.6.31/mountain.png</em></p></td><td><p><strong>T1486</strong> - Data Encrypted for Impact<br><em>This ransomware uses a combination of AES and RSA to encrypt files and protect its key. A noteworthy trait of this ransomware is that the key it uses for file encryption is derived from the C&C which is saved as a PNG file, even though it is not actually a PNG file.</em></p><p><strong>T1489</strong> - Service Stop<br><em>This ransomware attempts to stop certain processes using Microsoft Restart Manager<br><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Smss </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>anydesk </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Chrome </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Opera </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Msedge </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Firefox </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Iexplore </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Explorer </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Winlogon </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>SearchIndexer </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>Wininit </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>SearchApp </em><em>•<span style="white-space: pre;" data-mce-style="white-space: pre;"> </span>SearchUI <br><br>It also stops certain services using sc.exe<br><br><em>•"C:\Windows\System32\sc.exe" config SQLTELEMETRY start= disabled </em><em>•"C:\Windows\System32\sc.exe" config SQLTELEMETRY$ECWDB2 start= disabled </em><em>•"C:\Windows\System32\sc.exe" config SQLWriter start= disabled </em><em>•"C:\Windows\System32\sc.exe" config SstpSvc start= disabled </em><em>•"C:\Windows\System32\sc.exe" config MBAMService start= disabled </em><em>•"C:\Windows\System32\sc.exe" config wuauserv start= disabled </em></em></em></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><h2 class="centeredBlock no-margin-top">Summary of malware, tools, and exploits used</h2><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-1-col-layout"><p class="no-margin-top">Security teams can watch for the presence of the following malware tools and exploits that are typically used in BlackByte attacks:</p></div></div></div><div class="tableWrapper"><table class="tableContentDarkTheme mitreTableStyle summaryToolsStyle mce-item-table"><thead><tr><th>Initial Access</th><th>Execution</th><th>Discovery</th><th>Lateral Movement</th><th>Collection</th><th>Exfiltration</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><ul><li>ProxyShell</li></ul></td><td><ul><li>Certutil</li></ul></td><td><ul><li>NetScan</li></ul></td><td><ul><li>AnyDesk</li></ul></td><td><ul><li><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Calibri',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: Calibri; mso-fareast-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: AR-SA; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;" data-mce-style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Calibri',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: Calibri; mso-fareast-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: AR-SA; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">WinRAR</span></li></ul></td><td><p>Exfiltrates to the following C&C</p><ul><li>anonymfiles[.]com</li><li>file[.]io</li></ul></td></tr><tr><td><ul><li>China Chopper web shell</li></ul></td><td><ul><li>Cobeacon</li></ul></td><td></td><td><ul style="width: 179.1px; font-size: 14px;" data-mce-style="width: 179.1px; font-size: 14px;"><li style="margin-left: 7.35px;" data-mce-style="margin-left: 7.35px;">Cobeacon</li></ul></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><br></div></div><h2 class="centeredBlock no-margin-top">Recommendations</h2><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-1-col-layout"><p>Organizations face both established ransomware families as well as newer variants that are just entering the fray. Like many newer ransomware families, BlackByte is readying itself to take the spot of any big-game ransomware operation in decline. However, underneath it all could be a more intricate scheme of threat groups dispersing under new monikers. </p><p>As with the case of BlackByte, knowing its notable tactics, while also staying knowledgeable of bigger trends can help organizations create an effective strategy for ransomware attacks. In the case of BlackByte, prevention is key by keeping employees wary of phishing tactics and keeping up with security patches such as those for ProxyShell vulnerabilities.</p><p>To help defend systems against similar threats, organizations can establish security frameworks that can allocate resources systematically for establishing solid defenses against ransomware.</p><p>Here are some best practices that can be included in these frameworks:</p><div><br></div></div><div class="grid-3-col-layout darkGrid margin-topAdjust best-practices-grid"><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder inventory-icon"><br></div><h4>Audit and inventory</h4><ul><li>Take an inventory of assets and data</li><li>Identify authorized and unauthorized devices and software</li><li>Make an audit of event and incident logs</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder configure-icon"><br></div><h4>Configure and monitor</h4><ul><li>Manage hardware and software configurations</li><li>Grant admin privileges and access only when necessary to an employee’s role</li><li>Monitor network ports, protocols, and services</li><li>Activate security configurations on network infrastructure devices such as firewalls and routers</li><li>Establish a software allowlist that only executes legitimate applications</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder patch-icon"><br></div><h4>Patch and update</h4><ul><li>Conduct regular vulnerability assessments</li><li>Perform patching or virtual patching for operating systems and applications</li><li>Update software and applications to their latest versions</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder protect-icon"><br></div><h4>Protect and recover</h4><ul><li>Implement data protection, back up, and recovery measures</li><li>Enable multifactor authentication (MFA)</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder secure-icon"><br></div><h4>Secure and defend</h4><ul><li>Employ sandbox analysis to block malicious emails</li><li>Deploy the latest versions of security solutions to all layers of the system, including email, endpoint, web, and network</li><li>Detect early signs of an attack such as the presence of suspicious tools in the system</li><li>Use advanced detection technologies such as those powered by AI and machine learning</li></ul></div><div class="grid-col-layout"><div class="iconContainerHolder test-icon"><br></div><h4>Train and test</h4><ul><li>Regularly train and assess employees' security skills</li><li>Conduct red-team exercises and penetration tests</li></ul></div></div><div class="grid-1-col-layout"><p>A multilayered approach can help organizations guard possible entry points into the system (endpoint, email, web, and network). Security solutions that can detect malicious components and suspicious behavior can also help protect enterprises.</p><ul><li><a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/detection-response.html" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/detection-response.html">Trend Micro Vision One™</a> provides multilayered protection and behavior detection, which helps block questionable behavior and tools early on before the ransomware can do irreversible damage to the system.</li><li><a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/hybrid-cloud/cloud-one-workload-security.html" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/hybrid-cloud/cloud-one-workload-security.html">Trend Micro Cloud One™ Workload Security</a> protects systems against both known and unknown threats that exploit vulnerabilities. This protection is made possible through techniques such as virtual patching and machine learning. </li><li><a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/user-protection/sps/email-and-collaboration/email-inspector.html" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/user-protection/sps/email-and-collaboration/email-inspector.html">Trend Micro™ Deep Discovery™ Email Inspector</a> employs custom sandboxing and advanced analysis techniques to effectively block malicious emails, including phishing emails that can serve as entry points for ransomware.</li><li><a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/user-protection/sps/endpoint.html" data-mce-href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/user-protection/sps/endpoint.html">Trend Micro Apex One™</a> offers next-level automated threat detection and response against advanced concerns such as fileless threats and ransomware, ensuring the protection of endpoints.</li></ul></div></div></div><h2 class="centeredBlock no-margin-top">Indicators of Compromise (IOCs)</h2><div class="width-90-wide"><div class="wide-padding"><div class="grid-1-col-layout"><div class="grid-col"><p style="margin-top: -20px;" data-mce-style="margin-top: -20px;">The IOCs for this article can be found <a href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/ioc_spotlight_blackbyteXwCUeHS.txt" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mce-href="https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/TEx/articles/ioc_spotlight_blackbyteXwCUeHS.txt">here</a>. Actual indicators might vary per attack.</p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>
